      <p>The <b>Republic of the Congo</b> (<span style="font-size:85%;"><span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:En-ROC-pronunciation.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20"></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/c0/En-ROC-pronunciation.ogg" class="internal" title="En-ROC-pronunciation.ogg">pronunciation</a></span>&nbsp;<small class="metadata audiolinkinfo" style="cursor:help;">(<a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:Media help"><span style="cursor:help;">help</span></a>·<a href="/wiki/File:En-ROC-pronunciation.ogg" title="File:En-ROC-pronunciation.ogg"><span style="cursor:help;">info</span></a>)</small></span></span> <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <i lang="fr">République du Congo</i>, <a href="/wiki/Kituba_language" title="Kituba language">Kituba</a>: <i lang="mkw">Repubilika ya Kôngo</i>), also known as <b>Congo-Brazzaville</b>, the <b>Congo Republic</b><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ambacongofr.org_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ambacongofr.org-9">[9]</a></sup> or simply either <b>Congo</b> or <b>the Congo</b> is a country located in the western coast of <a href="/wiki/Central_Africa" title="Central Africa">Central Africa</a>. To the west lies <a href="/wiki/Gabon" title="Gabon">Gabon</a>; <a href="/wiki/Cameroon" title="Cameroon">Cameroon</a> to its northwest and the <a href="/wiki/Central_African_Republic" title="Central African Republic">Central African Republic</a> to its northeast; the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">Democratic Republic of the Congo</a> to the southeast and the <a href="/wiki/Angola" title="Angola">Angolan</a> <a href="/wiki/Exclave" class="mw-redirect" title="Exclave">exclave</a> of <a href="/wiki/Cabinda_Province" title="Cabinda Province">Cabinda</a> to its south; and the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a> to its southwest. The official language is <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>. </p>
      <p>The region was dominated by <a href="/wiki/Bantu_peoples" title="Bantu peoples">Bantu</a>-speaking tribes at least 3,000 years ago, who built trade links leading into the <a href="/wiki/Congo_River" title="Congo River">Congo River</a> basin. Congo was formerly part of the <a href="/wiki/French_colonial_empire" title="French colonial empire">French colony</a> of <a href="/wiki/French_Equatorial_Africa" title="French Equatorial Africa">Equatorial Africa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-10">[10]</a></sup> The Republic of the Congo was established on 28 November 1958 and gained independence from France in 1960. It was a <a href="/wiki/Marxist%E2%80%93Leninist" class="mw-redirect" title="Marxist–Leninist">Marxist–Leninist</a> state from 1969 to 1992, under the name <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="People's Republic of the Congo">People's Republic of the Congo</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">sovereign state</a> has had multi-party elections since 1992, although a democratically elected government was ousted in the 1997 <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_the_Congo_Civil_War_(1997%E2%80%9399)" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of the Congo Civil War (1997–99)">Republic of the Congo Civil War</a>, and President <a href="/wiki/Denis_Sassou_Nguesso" title="Denis Sassou Nguesso">Denis Sassou Nguesso</a>, who first came to power in 1979, has ruled for 35 of the past 40 years. </p>
      <p>The Republic of the Congo is a member of the <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">African Union</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, <a href="/wiki/La_Francophonie" class="mw-redirect" title="La Francophonie">La Francophonie</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Economic_Community_of_Central_African_States" title="Economic Community of Central African States">Economic Community of Central African States</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement" title="Non-Aligned Movement">Non-Aligned Movement</a>. It has become the fourth-largest <a href="/wiki/Oil_producer" class="mw-redirect" title="Oil producer">oil producer</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Guinea" title="Gulf of Guinea">Gulf of Guinea</a>, providing the country with a degree of prosperity despite political and economic instability in some areas and unequal distribution of oil revenue nationwide. <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_the_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Economy of the Republic of the Congo">Congo's economy</a> is heavily dependent on the oil sector, and economic growth has slowed considerably since <a href="/wiki/2010s_oil_glut" title="2010s oil glut">the post-2015 drop in oil prices</a>. With a population of 5.2 million, 88.5% of the country practices <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_the_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Religion in the Republic of the Congo">Christianity</a>. </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>The country’s name means "[Land beside] the <a href="/wiki/Congo_River" title="Congo River">Congo River</a>", adopted by the country upon independence in 1960 from the previous <a href="/wiki/Fifth_French_Republic" class="mw-redirect" title="Fifth French Republic">French</a> autonomous colony Republic of the Congo (<a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <i lang="fr">République du Congo</i>) established in 1958, ultimately from the name of the original <a href="/wiki/Third_French_Republic" class="mw-redirect" title="Third French Republic">French</a> <a href="/wiki/List_of_French_colonies" class="mw-redirect" title="List of French colonies">colony</a> <a href="/wiki/French_Congo" title="French Congo">French Congo</a> (<i lang="fr" title="French-language text">Congo français</i>) established in 1882. The river itself derived its name from <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Kongo" title="Kingdom of Kongo">Kongo</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Bantu_peoples" title="Bantu peoples">Bantu</a> kingdom which occupied its mouth around the time of its discovery by the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Portugal" title="Kingdom of Portugal">Portuguese</a> in 1483<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> or 1484<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> and whose name derived from its people, the <a href="/wiki/Bakongo" class="mw-redirect" title="Bakongo">Bakongo</a>, an endonym said to mean "hunters" (<a href="/wiki/Kongo_language" title="Kongo language">Kongo</a>: <i lang="kg">mukongo</i>, <i>nkongo</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Other names are sometimes known to as the <a href="/wiki/French_Congo" title="French Congo">French Congo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Middle_Congo" class="mw-redirect" title="Middle Congo">Middle Congo</a> and Congo (Brazzaville) with the latter inclusion of the country's capital to distinguish it from <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">Congo (Léopoldville)</a> or (Kinshasa) to its south. <a href="/wiki/Brazzaville" title="Brazzaville">Brazzaville</a> itself derives from the colony's founder, <a href="/wiki/Pierre_Savorgnan_de_Brazza" title="Pierre Savorgnan de Brazza">Pierre Savorgnan de Brazzà</a>, an Italian nobleman whose title referred to the town of Brazzacco, in the <a href="/wiki/Comune" title="Comune">comune</a> of <a href="/wiki/Moruzzo" title="Moruzzo">Moruzzo</a>, whose name derived from the <a href="/wiki/Latin_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Latin language">Latin</a> <i>Brattius</i> or <i>Braccius</i>, both meaning "arm".<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="History of the Republic of the Congo">History of the Republic of the Congo</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-colonial">Pre-colonial</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Pre-colonial">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Bantu_peoples" title="Bantu peoples">Bantu-speaking peoples</a> who founded tribes during the <a href="/wiki/Bantu_expansion" title="Bantu expansion">Bantu expansions</a> largely displaced and absorbed the earliest inhabitants of the region, the <a href="/wiki/African_Pygmies" title="African Pygmies">Pygmy</a> people, about 1500<span class="nowrap">&nbsp;</span>BC. The <a href="/wiki/Bakongo" class="mw-redirect" title="Bakongo">Bakongo</a>, a Bantu ethnic group that also occupied parts of present-day Angola, Gabon, and the Democratic Republic of the Congo, formed the basis for ethnic affinities and rivalries among those countries. Several Bantu kingdoms—notably those of the <a href="/wiki/Kongo_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Kongo Empire">Kongo</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Loango" title="Kingdom of Loango">Loango</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Anziku" class="mw-redirect" title="Kingdom of Anziku">Teke</a>—built trade links leading into the Congo River basin.<sup id="cite_ref-dos2009_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dos2009-15">[15]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Portugal" title="Kingdom of Portugal">Portuguese</a> <a href="/wiki/Explorer" class="mw-redirect" title="Explorer">explorer</a> <a href="/wiki/Diogo_C%C3%A3o" title="Diogo Cão">Diogo Cão</a> reached the mouth of the Congo in 1484.<sup id="cite_ref-DicImp_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DicImp-16">[16]</a></sup> Commercial relationships quickly grew between the inland Bantu kingdoms and European merchants who traded in various commodities, manufactured goods, and also people captured and enslaved in the <a href="/wiki/Hinterland" title="Hinterland">hinterlands</a>. After centuries as a major hub for transatlantic trade, direct European colonization of the Congo river delta began in the late 19th century, subsequently eroding the power of the Bantu societies in the region.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="French_colonial_era">French colonial era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: French colonial era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/French_Congo" title="French Congo">French Congo</a> and <a href="/wiki/French_Equatorial_Africa" title="French Equatorial Africa">French Equatorial Africa</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Court_of_Loango.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Court_of_Loango.png/220px-Court_of_Loango.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="149" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Court_of_Loango.png/330px-Court_of_Loango.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Court_of_Loango.png/440px-Court_of_Loango.png 2x" data-file-width="1276" data-file-height="862"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Court_of_Loango.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The court of <a href="/wiki/N%27Gangue_M%27voumbe_Niambi" title="N'Gangue M'voumbe Niambi">N'Gangue M'voumbe Niambi</a>, from the book <i>Description of Africa</i> (1668)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The area north of the Congo River came under French sovereignty in 1880 as a result of <a href="/wiki/Pierre_de_Brazza" class="mw-redirect" title="Pierre de Brazza">Pierre de Brazza</a>'s treaty with King Makoko<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> of the <a href="/wiki/Bateke" class="mw-redirect" title="Bateke">Bateke</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DicImp_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DicImp-16">[16]</a></sup> After the death of Makoko, his widow Queen Ngalifourou upheld the terms of the treaty and became an important ally to the colonisers.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> This Congo Colony became known first as <a href="/wiki/French_Congo" title="French Congo">French Congo</a>, then as Middle Congo in 1903. </p>
      <p>In 1908, France organized <a href="/wiki/French_Equatorial_Africa" title="French Equatorial Africa">French Equatorial Africa</a> (AEF), comprising the Middle Congo, <a href="/wiki/French_Gabon" class="mw-redirect" title="French Gabon">Gabon</a>, <a href="/wiki/French_Chad" title="French Chad">Chad</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Oubangui-Chari" class="mw-redirect" title="Oubangui-Chari">Oubangui-Chari</a> (the modern <a href="/wiki/Central_African_Republic" title="Central African Republic">Central African Republic</a>). The French designated <a href="/wiki/Brazzaville" title="Brazzaville">Brazzaville</a> as the federal capital. Economic development during the first 50 years of colonial rule in Congo centered on natural-resource extraction. The methods were often brutal: construction of the <a href="/wiki/Congo-Ocean_Railway" class="mw-redirect" title="Congo-Ocean Railway">Congo-Ocean Railway</a> following <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a> has been estimated to have cost at least 14,000 lives.<sup id="cite_ref-DicImp_16-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DicImp-16">[16]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>During the <a href="/wiki/Nazi_occupation_of_France" class="mw-redirect" title="Nazi occupation of France">Nazi occupation of France</a> during <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, Brazzaville functioned as the symbolic capital of <a href="/wiki/Free_France" title="Free France">Free France</a> between 1940 and 1943.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Brazzaville_Conference_of_1944" class="mw-redirect" title="Brazzaville Conference of 1944">Brazzaville Conference of 1944</a> heralded a period of major reform in French colonial policy. Congo benefited from the postwar expansion of colonial administrative and infrastructure spending as a result of its central geographic location within AEF and the federal capital at Brazzaville.<sup id="cite_ref-dos2009_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dos2009-15">[15]</a></sup> It also had a local legislature after the adoption of the 1946 constitution that established the <a href="/wiki/French_Fourth_Republic" title="French Fourth Republic">Fourth Republic</a>. </p>
      <p>Following the revision of the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_France" title="Constitution of France">French constitution</a> that established the <a href="/wiki/French_Fifth_Republic" title="French Fifth Republic">Fifth Republic</a> in 1958, the AEF dissolved into its constituent parts, each of which became an autonomous colony within the <a href="/wiki/French_Community" title="French Community">French Community</a>. During these reforms, Middle Congo became known as the Republic of the Congo in 1958<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> and published its first constitution in 1959.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> Antagonism between the <a href="/wiki/Mbochi" class="mw-redirect" title="Mbochi">Mbochis</a> (who favored <a href="/wiki/Jacques_Opangault" title="Jacques Opangault">Jacques Opangault</a>) and the <a href="/wiki/Lari_people_(Congo)" title="Lari people (Congo)">Laris</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kongo_people" title="Kongo people">Kongos</a> (who favored <a href="/wiki/Fulbert_Youlou" title="Fulbert Youlou">Fulbert Youlou</a>, the first black mayor elected in French Equatorial Africa) resulted in a series of riots in Brazzaville in February 1959, which the <a href="/wiki/French_Army" title="French Army">French Army</a> subdued.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>New elections took place in April 1959. By the time the Congo became independent in August 1960, Opangault, the former opponent of Youlou, agreed to serve under him. Youlou became the first President of the Republic of the Congo.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> Since the political tension was so high in <a href="/wiki/Pointe-Noire" title="Pointe-Noire">Pointe-Noire</a>, Youlou moved the capital to Brazzaville. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-independence_era">Post-independence era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Post-independence era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:214px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Alphonse_Massamba-Debat.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/2d/Alphonse_Massamba-Debat.png" decoding="async" width="212" height="286" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="212" data-file-height="286"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Alphonse_Massamba-Debat.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Alphonse_Massamba-D%C3%A9bat" title="Alphonse Massamba-Débat">Alphonse Massamba-Débat</a>'s one-party rule (1963–1968) attempted to implement a <a href="/wiki/Political_economy" title="Political economy">political economic</a> strategy of "<a href="/wiki/Scientific_socialism" title="Scientific socialism">scientific socialism</a>"
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Republic of the Congo became fully independent from France on 15 August 1960. Youlou ruled as the country's first president until labour elements and rival political parties instigated a <a href="/wiki/Trois_Glorieuses_(1963)" title="Trois Glorieuses (1963)">three-day uprising</a> that ousted him.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> The Congolese military briefly took over the country, and installed a civilian provisional government headed by <a href="/wiki/Alphonse_Massamba-D%C3%A9bat" title="Alphonse Massamba-Débat">Alphonse Massamba-Débat</a>. </p>
      <p>Under the 1963 constitution, Massamba-Débat was elected President for a five-year term.<sup id="cite_ref-dos2009_15-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dos2009-15">[15]</a></sup> During <a href="/wiki/Alphonse_Massamba-D%C3%A9bat#Congo_under_Massamba-Débat_(1963-1968)" title="Alphonse Massamba-Débat">Massamba-Débat's term in office</a> the regime adopted "<a href="/wiki/Scientific_socialism" title="Scientific socialism">scientific socialism</a>" as the country's constitutional ideology.<sup id="cite_ref-shillington301_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shillington301-26">[26]</a></sup> In 1965, Congo established relations with the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>, the <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">People's Republic of China</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Korea" title="North Korea">North Korea</a> and <a href="/wiki/North_Vietnam" title="North Vietnam">North Vietnam</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-shillington301_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shillington301-26">[26]</a></sup> On the night of February 14 to 15, 1965, three prominent public officials of the Republic of the Congo were kidnapped: <a href="/w/index.php?title=Lazare_Matsocota&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Lazare Matsocota (page does not exist)">Lazare Matsocota</a> (prosecutor of the Republic), <a href="/w/index.php?title=Joseph_Pouabou&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Joseph Pouabou (page does not exist)">Joseph Pouabou</a> (president of the Supreme Court) and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Massou%C3%A9m%C3%A9_Anselme&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Massouémé Anselme (page does not exist)">Massouémé Anselme</a> (director of the Congolese Information Agency). The bodies of two of these men were later found, mutilated, by the <a href="/wiki/Congo_River" title="Congo River">Congo River</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> Massamba-Débat's regime also invited several hundred <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuban</a> army troops into the country to train his party's militia units and these troops helped his government survive a <a href="/wiki/1966_Republic_of_the_Congo_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat_attempt" title="1966 Republic of the Congo coup d'état attempt"><i>coup d'état</i> in 1966</a> led by paratroopers loyal to future President <a href="/wiki/Marien_Ngouabi" title="Marien Ngouabi">Marien Ngouabi</a>. Nevertheless, Massamba-Débat was unable to reconcile various institutional, tribal and ideological factions within the country<sup id="cite_ref-shillington301_26-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shillington301-26">[26]</a></sup> and his regime ended abruptly with a bloodless <a href="/wiki/1968_Republic_of_the_Congo_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="1968 Republic of the Congo coup d'état"><i>coup</i> in September 1968</a>. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Congo_1972_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Congo_1972_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-Congo_1972_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="272" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/45/Congo_1972_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="252" data-file-height="311"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Congo_1972_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Marien_Ngouabi" title="Marien Ngouabi">Marien Ngouabi</a> changed the country's name to the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="People's Republic of the Congo">People's Republic of the Congo</a>, declaring it <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a>'s first Marxist–Leninist state. He was assassinated in 1977.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Marie Ngouabi, who had participated in the coup, assumed the presidency on 31 December 1968. One year later, Ngouabi proclaimed the Congo Africa's first "people's republic", the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="People's Republic of the Congo">People's Republic of the Congo</a>, and announced the decision of the National Revolutionary Movement to change its name to the <a href="/wiki/Congolese_Party_of_Labour" title="Congolese Party of Labour">Congolese Labour Party</a> (PCT). He survived an <a href="/wiki/1972_Republic_of_the_Congo_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat_attempt" title="1972 Republic of the Congo coup d'état attempt">attempted <i>coup</i> in 1972</a> but was assassinated on 16 March<span class="nowrap">&nbsp;</span>1977. An 11-member Military Committee of the Party (CMP) was then named to head an interim government, with <a href="/wiki/Joachim_Yhombi-Opango" title="Joachim Yhombi-Opango">Joachim Yhombi-Opango</a> serving as president. Two years later, Yhombi-Opango was forced from power and <a href="/wiki/Denis_Sassou_Nguesso" title="Denis Sassou Nguesso">Denis Sassou Nguesso</a> become the new president.<sup id="cite_ref-dos2009_15-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dos2009-15">[15]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Sassou Nguesso aligned the country with the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Bloc" title="Eastern Bloc">Eastern Bloc</a> and signed a twenty-year friendship pact with the Soviet Union. Over the years, Sassou had to rely more on <a href="/wiki/Political_repression" title="Political repression">political repression</a> and less on <a href="/wiki/Patronage" title="Patronage">patronage</a> to maintain his dictatorship.<sup id="cite_ref-shillington302_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shillington302-29">[29]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Pascal_Lissouba" title="Pascal Lissouba">Pascal Lissouba</a>, who became Congo's first elected president (1992–1997) during the period of multi-party democracy, attempted to implement economic reforms with IMF backing to liberalize the economy. In June 1996, the IMF approved a three-year <a href="/wiki/Special_drawing_rights" title="Special drawing rights">SDR</a>69.5m (US$100m) enhanced structural adjustment facility (ESAF) and was on the verge of announcing a renewed annual agreement when civil war broke out in Congo in mid-1997.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Congo's democratic progress was derailed in 1997, when Lissouba and Sassou started to fight for power in the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_the_Congo_Civil_War_(1997-99)" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of the Congo Civil War (1997-99)">civil war</a>. As presidential elections scheduled for July 1997 approached, tensions between the Lissouba and Sassou camps mounted. On 5 June, President Lissouba's government forces surrounded Sassou's compound in Brazzaville and Sassou ordered members of his private militia (known as "Cobras") to resist. Thus began a four-month conflict that destroyed or damaged much of Brazzaville and caused tens of thousands of civilian deaths. In early October, the Angolan government began an invasion of Congo to install Sassou in power. In mid-October, the Lissouba government fell. Soon thereafter, Sassou declared himself president.<sup id="cite_ref-dos2009_15-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dos2009-15">[15]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Pro-constitutional_reform_demonstration_in_Brazzaville_-_2015-10_(21518932913).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Pro-constitutional_reform_demonstration_in_Brazzaville_-_2015-10_%2821518932913%29.jpg/220px-Pro-constitutional_reform_demonstration_in_Brazzaville_-_2015-10_%2821518932913%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Pro-constitutional_reform_demonstration_in_Brazzaville_-_2015-10_%2821518932913%29.jpg/330px-Pro-constitutional_reform_demonstration_in_Brazzaville_-_2015-10_%2821518932913%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Pro-constitutional_reform_demonstration_in_Brazzaville_-_2015-10_%2821518932913%29.jpg/440px-Pro-constitutional_reform_demonstration_in_Brazzaville_-_2015-10_%2821518932913%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1599" data-file-height="899"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Pro-constitutional_reform_demonstration_in_Brazzaville_-_2015-10_(21518932913).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A pro-constitutional reform rally in Brazzaville during October 2015. The constitution's controversial reforms were subsequently approved in a disputed election which saw demonstrations and violence.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In the controversial <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_the_Congo_presidential_election,_2002" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of the Congo presidential election, 2002">elections in 2002</a>, Sassou won with almost 90% of the vote cast. His two main rivals, Lissouba and Bernard Kolelas, were prevented from competing and the only remaining credible rival, <a href="/wiki/Andr%C3%A9_Milongo" title="André Milongo">André Milongo</a>, advised his supporters to boycott the elections and then withdrew from the race.<sup id="cite_ref-freedomhouse_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-freedomhouse-31">[31]</a></sup> A new <a href="/wiki/Constitution" title="Constitution">constitution</a>, agreed upon by <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_the_Congo_constitutional_referendum,_2002" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of the Congo constitutional referendum, 2002">referendum in January 2002</a>, granted the president new powers, extended his term to seven years, and introduced a new bicameral assembly. International observers took issue with the organization of the presidential election and the constitutional referendum, both of which were reminiscent in their organization of Congo's era of the one-party state.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> Following the presidential elections, fighting restarted in the <a href="/wiki/Pool_Department" title="Pool Department">Pool region</a> between government forces and rebels led by <a href="/wiki/Pastor_Ntumi" class="mw-redirect" title="Pastor Ntumi">Pastor Ntumi</a>; a peace treaty to end the conflict was signed in April 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Sassou also won the following <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_the_Congo_presidential_election,_2009" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of the Congo presidential election, 2009">presidential election in July 2009</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> According to the Congolese Observatory of Human Rights, a non-governmental organization, the election was marked by "very low" turnout and "fraud and irregularities".<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> In March 2015 Sassou announced that he wanted to run for yet another term in office and a <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_the_Congo_constitutional_referendum,_2015" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of the Congo constitutional referendum, 2015">constitutional referendum</a> in October resulted in a changed constitution which allowed him to run during the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_the_Congo_presidential_election,_2016" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of the Congo presidential election, 2016">2016 presidential election</a>. He won the election believed by many to be fraudulent. After violent protests in the capital, Sassou attacked the Pool region, where the <a href="/wiki/Ninja_(militia)" title="Ninja (militia)">Ninja rebels</a> of the civil war used to be based, in what was believed to be a distraction. This led to a revival of the Ninja rebels who launched attacks against the army in April 2016, leading 80,000 people to flee their homes. A ceasefire deal was signed in December 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Denis_Sassou-Nguesso.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Denis_Sassou-Nguesso.jpg/220px-Denis_Sassou-Nguesso.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="324" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/48/Denis_Sassou-Nguesso.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="316" data-file-height="466"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Denis_Sassou-Nguesso.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Denis_Sassou_Nguesso" title="Denis Sassou Nguesso">Denis Sassou Nguesso</a> served as President from 1979 to 1992 and has remained in power ever since his rebel forces ousted President <a href="/wiki/Pascal_Lissouba" title="Pascal Lissouba">Pascal Lissouba</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_the_Congo_Civil_War_(1997-99)" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of the Congo Civil War (1997-99)">1997 Civil War</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_the_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Politics of the Republic of the Congo">Politics of the Republic of the Congo</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_the_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Foreign relations of the Republic of the Congo">Foreign relations of the Republic of the Congo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Military_of_the_Republic_of_the_Congo" class="mw-redirect" title="Military of the Republic of the Congo">Military of the Republic of the Congo</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Biens_mal_acquis" title="Biens mal acquis">Biens mal acquis</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Congo-Brazzaville has had a <a href="/wiki/Multi-party_system" title="Multi-party system">multi-party political system</a> since the early 1990s, although the system is heavily dominated by President <a href="/wiki/Denis_Sassou_Nguesso" title="Denis Sassou Nguesso">Denis Sassou Nguesso</a>; he has lacked serious competition in the presidential elections held under his rule. Sassou Nguesso is backed by his own <a href="/wiki/Congolese_Labour_Party" class="mw-redirect" title="Congolese Labour Party">Congolese Labour Party</a> (<a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <i lang="fr">Parti Congolais du Travail</i>) as well as a range of smaller parties. </p>
      <p>Sassou's regime has seen many <a href="/wiki/Political_corruption" title="Political corruption"> corruption</a> revelations despite attempts to censor them. One French investigation found over 110 bank accounts and dozens of lavish properties in France.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> Sassou denounced embezzlement investigations as "racist" and "colonial".<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> Denis Christel Sassou-Nguesso, son of Denis Sassou Nguesso, has been named in association with the <a href="/wiki/Panama_Papers" title="Panama Papers">Panama Papers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 27 March 2015, Sassou Nguesso announced that his government would hold a referendum on changing the country's 2002 constitution to allow him to run for a third consecutive term in office.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> On 25 October the government held a referendum on allowing Sassou Nguesso to run in the next election. The government claimed that the proposal was approved by 92% of voters, with 72% of eligible voters participating. The opposition, who boycotted the referendum, said that the government's statistics were false and the vote was a fake one.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The election raised questions and was accompanied by civil unrest and police shootings of protesters;<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> at least 18 people were killed by security forces during opposition rallies leading up to the referendum held in October. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Media_of_the_Republic_of_the_Congo" class="mw-redirect" title="Media of the Republic of the Congo">Media of the Republic of the Congo</a>
      </div> 
      <p>In 2008, the primary media were owned by the government, but privately run forms of media were being created. There is one government-owned television station and around 10 small private television channels. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights">Human rights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Human rights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_the_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Human rights in the Republic of the Congo">Human rights in the Republic of the Congo</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Many <a href="/wiki/Pygmies" class="mw-redirect" title="Pygmies">Pygmies</a> belong from birth to <a href="/wiki/Bantu_peoples" title="Bantu peoples">Bantus</a> in a relationship many refer to as slavery.<sup id="cite_ref-globalpost_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-globalpost-45">[45]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-internationalreportingproject_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-internationalreportingproject-46">[46]</a></sup> The Congolese Human Rights Observatory says that the Pygmies are treated as property in the same way as pets.<sup id="cite_ref-globalpost_45-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-globalpost-45">[45]</a></sup> On 30 December<span class="nowrap">&nbsp;</span>2010, the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_the_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Parliament of the Republic of the Congo">Congolese parliament</a> adopted a law for to promote and protect the rights of indigenous peoples.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (October 2019)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> This law is the first of its kind in Africa, and its adoption is a historic development for indigenous peoples on the continent.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The text near this tag is dated. (October 2019)">needs update</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Congo_departments_named.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Congo_departments_named.png/250px-Congo_departments_named.png" decoding="async" width="250" height="315" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/ad/Congo_departments_named.png 1.5x" data-file-width="298" data-file-height="375"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Congo_departments_named.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Map of the Republic of the Congo exhibiting its twelve departments.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Departments_of_the_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Departments of the Republic of the Congo">Departments of the Republic of the Congo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Communes_of_the_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Communes of the Republic of the Congo">Communes of the Republic of the Congo</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_the_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Districts of the Republic of the Congo">Districts of the Republic of the Congo</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The Republic of the Congo is divided into 12 <a href="/wiki/Departments_of_the_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Departments of the Republic of the Congo"><i>départements</i></a> (departments). Departments are divided into communes and districts.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> These are: </p> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r998391716">.mw-parser-output .div-col{margin-top:0.3em;column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .div-col-small{font-size:90%}.mw-parser-output .div-col-rules{column-rule:1px solid #aaa}.mw-parser-output .div-col dl,.mw-parser-output .div-col ol,.mw-parser-output .div-col ul{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .div-col li,.mw-parser-output .div-col dd{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}</style>
      <div class="div-col" style="column-width: 10em;"> 
       <ul>
        <li><a href="/wiki/Bouenza_Department" title="Bouenza Department">Bouenza</a></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Brazzaville" title="Brazzaville">Brazzaville</a></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Cuvette_Department" title="Cuvette Department">Cuvette</a></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Cuvette-Ouest_Department" title="Cuvette-Ouest Department">Cuvette-Ouest</a></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Kouilou_Department" title="Kouilou Department">Kouilou</a></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/L%C3%A9koumou_Department" title="Lékoumou Department">Lékoumou</a></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Likouala_Department" title="Likouala Department">Likouala</a></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Niari_Department" title="Niari Department">Niari</a></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Plateaux_Department_(Republic_of_the_Congo)" title="Plateaux Department (Republic of the Congo)">Plateaux</a></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Pointe-Noire" title="Pointe-Noire">Pointe-Noire</a></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Pool_Department" title="Pool Department">Pool</a></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Sangha_Department_(Republic_of_the_Congo)" title="Sangha Department (Republic of the Congo)">Sangha</a></li>
       </ul>
      </div> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography_and_climate">Geography and climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Geography and climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_the_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Geography of the Republic of the Congo">Geography of the Republic of the Congo</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Climate_Brazzaville.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Climate_Brazzaville.svg/290px-Climate_Brazzaville.svg.png" decoding="async" width="290" height="178" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Climate_Brazzaville.svg/435px-Climate_Brazzaville.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Climate_Brazzaville.svg/580px-Climate_Brazzaville.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="700" data-file-height="430"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Climate_Brazzaville.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Climate diagram for <a href="/wiki/Brazzaville" title="Brazzaville">Brazzaville</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Congo is located in the central-western part of <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">sub-Saharan Africa</a>, along the <a href="/wiki/Equator" title="Equator">Equator</a>, lying between latitudes <a href="/wiki/4th_parallel_north" title="4th parallel north">4°N</a> and <a href="/wiki/5th_parallel_south" title="5th parallel south">5°S</a>, and longitudes <a href="/wiki/11th_meridian_east" title="11th meridian east">11°</a> and <a href="/wiki/19th_meridian_east" title="19th meridian east">19°E</a>. To the south and east of it is the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">Democratic Republic of the Congo</a>. It is also bounded by <a href="/wiki/Gabon" title="Gabon">Gabon</a> to the west, <a href="/wiki/Cameroon" title="Cameroon">Cameroon</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Central_African_Republic" title="Central African Republic">Central African Republic</a> to the north, and <a href="/wiki/Cabinda_(province)" class="mw-redirect" title="Cabinda (province)">Cabinda</a> (<a href="/wiki/Angola" title="Angola">Angola</a>) to the southwest. It has a short coast on the Atlantic Ocean. </p>
      <p>The capital, <a href="/wiki/Brazzaville" title="Brazzaville">Brazzaville</a>, is located on the Congo River, in the south of the country, immediately across from <a href="/wiki/Kinshasa" title="Kinshasa">Kinshasa</a>, the capital of the Democratic Republic of the Congo. </p>
      <p>The southwest of the country is a coastal plain for which the primary drainage is the <a href="/wiki/Kouilou-Niari_River" title="Kouilou-Niari River">Kouilou-Niari River</a>; the interior of the country consists of a central plateau between two basins to the south and north. Forests are under increasing exploitation pressure.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> Congo had a 2018 <a href="/wiki/Forest_Landscape_Integrity_Index" title="Forest Landscape Integrity Index">Forest Landscape Integrity Index</a> mean score of 8.89/10, ranking it 12<sup>th</sup> globally out of 172 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-FLII-Supplementary_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FLII-Supplementary-50">[50]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Congo lies within four terrestrial ecoregions: <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Equatorial_coastal_forests" title="Atlantic Equatorial coastal forests">Atlantic Equatorial coastal forests</a>, <a href="/wiki/Northwestern_Congolian_lowland_forests" title="Northwestern Congolian lowland forests">Northwestern Congolian lowland forests</a>, <a href="/wiki/Western_Congolian_swamp_forests" title="Western Congolian swamp forests">Western Congolian swamp forests</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Western_Congolian_forest-savanna_mosaic" title="Western Congolian forest-savanna mosaic">Western Congolian forest-savanna mosaic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DinersteinOlson2017_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DinersteinOlson2017-51">[51]</a></sup> Since the country is located on the Equator, the climate is consistent year-round, with the average day temperature a humid 24&nbsp;°C (75&nbsp;°F) and nights generally between 16&nbsp;°C (61&nbsp;°F) and 21&nbsp;°C (70&nbsp;°F). The average yearly rainfall ranges from 1,100 millimetres (43&nbsp;in) in the <a href="/wiki/Niari_Valley" title="Niari Valley">Niari Valley</a> in the south to over 2,000 millimetres (79&nbsp;in) in central parts of the country. The dry season is from June to August, while in the majority of the country the wet season has two rainfall maxima: one in March–May and another in September–November.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2006–07, researchers from the <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_Conservation_Society" title="Wildlife Conservation Society">Wildlife Conservation Society</a> studied gorillas in heavily forested regions centered on the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ouesso_district&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Ouesso district (page does not exist)">Ouesso district</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Sangha_Region" class="mw-redirect" title="Sangha Region">Sangha Region</a>. They suggest a population on the order of 125,000 <a href="/wiki/Western_lowland_gorilla" title="Western lowland gorilla">western lowland gorillas</a>, whose isolation from humans has been largely preserved by inhospitable swamps.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_the_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Economy of the Republic of the Congo">Economy of the Republic of the Congo</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Hydrocarbon_exploration" title="Hydrocarbon exploration">Hydrocarbon exploration</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_companies_based_in_the_Republic_of_the_Congo" class="mw-redirect" title="List of companies based in the Republic of the Congo">List of companies based in the Republic of the Congo</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Manihot_esculenta_-_K%C3%B6hler%E2%80%93s_Medizinal-Pflanzen-090.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Manihot_esculenta_-_K%C3%B6hler%E2%80%93s_Medizinal-Pflanzen-090.jpg/170px-Manihot_esculenta_-_K%C3%B6hler%E2%80%93s_Medizinal-Pflanzen-090.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Manihot_esculenta_-_K%C3%B6hler%E2%80%93s_Medizinal-Pflanzen-090.jpg/255px-Manihot_esculenta_-_K%C3%B6hler%E2%80%93s_Medizinal-Pflanzen-090.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Manihot_esculenta_-_K%C3%B6hler%E2%80%93s_Medizinal-Pflanzen-090.jpg/340px-Manihot_esculenta_-_K%C3%B6hler%E2%80%93s_Medizinal-Pflanzen-090.jpg 2x" data-file-width="460" data-file-height="594"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Manihot_esculenta_-_K%C3%B6hler%E2%80%93s_Medizinal-Pflanzen-090.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Cassava" title="Cassava">Cassava</a> is an important food crop in the Republic of the Congo.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The economy is a mixture of village agriculture and handicrafts, an industrial sector based largely on <a href="/wiki/Petroleum" title="Petroleum">petroleum</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-eia_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eia-54">[54]</a></sup> support services, and a government characterized by budget problems and overstaffing. Petroleum extraction has supplanted <a href="/wiki/Forestry" title="Forestry">forestry</a> as the mainstay of the economy. In 2008, the oil sector accounted for 65% of the <a href="/wiki/GDP" class="mw-redirect" title="GDP">GDP</a>, 85% of government revenue, and 92% of exports.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> The country also has large untapped <a href="/wiki/Mining_in_the_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Mining in the Republic of the Congo">mineral</a> wealth. </p>
      <p>In the early 1980s, rapidly rising oil revenues enabled the government to finance large-scale development projects. GDP grew an average 5% annually, one of the highest rates in Africa. The government has mortgaged a substantial portion of its petroleum earnings, contributing to a shortage of revenues. On 12 January<span class="nowrap">&nbsp;</span>1994 devaluation of <a href="/wiki/CFA_franc" title="CFA franc">Franc Zone</a> currencies by 50% resulted in inflation of 46% in 1994, but inflation has subsided since.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Jeunes_filles_apprenant_la_couture_-_Ecole_Sp%C3%A9ciale_de_Brazzaville.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Jeunes_filles_apprenant_la_couture_-_Ecole_Sp%C3%A9ciale_de_Brazzaville.jpg/220px-Jeunes_filles_apprenant_la_couture_-_Ecole_Sp%C3%A9ciale_de_Brazzaville.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="133" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Jeunes_filles_apprenant_la_couture_-_Ecole_Sp%C3%A9ciale_de_Brazzaville.jpg/330px-Jeunes_filles_apprenant_la_couture_-_Ecole_Sp%C3%A9ciale_de_Brazzaville.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Jeunes_filles_apprenant_la_couture_-_Ecole_Sp%C3%A9ciale_de_Brazzaville.jpg/440px-Jeunes_filles_apprenant_la_couture_-_Ecole_Sp%C3%A9ciale_de_Brazzaville.jpg 2x" data-file-width="566" data-file-height="341"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Jeunes_filles_apprenant_la_couture_-_Ecole_Sp%C3%A9ciale_de_Brazzaville.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Young women learning to sew, Brazzaville
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Economic reform efforts continued with the support of international organizations, notably the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> and the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a>. The reform program came to a halt in June 1997 when civil war erupted. When Sassou Nguesso returned to power at the end of the war in October 1997, he publicly expressed interest in moving forward on <a href="/wiki/Economic_reform" class="mw-redirect" title="Economic reform">economic reforms</a> and <a href="/wiki/Privatization" title="Privatization">privatization</a> and in renewing cooperation with international financial institutions. However, economic progress was badly hurt by slumping oil prices and the resumption of armed conflict in December 1998, which worsened the republic's budget deficit. </p>
      <p>The current administration presides over an uneasy internal peace and faces difficult economic problems of stimulating recovery and reducing poverty, despite record-high oil prices since 2003. Natural gas and diamonds are also recent major Congolese exports, although Congo was excluded from the <a href="/wiki/Kimberley_Process" class="mw-redirect" title="Kimberley Process">Kimberley Process</a> in 2004 amid allegations that most of its diamond exports were in fact being smuggled out of the neighboring <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">Democratic Republic of the Congo</a>; it was re-admitted to the group in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Republic of the Congo also has large untapped base metal, gold, iron and phosphate deposits.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> The country is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Organization_for_the_Harmonization_of_Business_Law_in_Africa" class="mw-redirect" title="Organization for the Harmonization of Business Law in Africa">Organization for the Harmonization of Business Law in Africa</a> (OHADA).<sup id="cite_ref-ohada.com_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ohada.com-60">[60]</a></sup> The Congolese government signed an agreement in 2009 to lease 200,000 hectares of land to <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South African</a> farmers to reduce its dependence on imports.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The GDP of the Republic of the Congo grew by 6% in 2014 and is expected to have grown by 7.5% in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2018, the Republic of the Congo joined the <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_Petroleum_Exporting_Countries" class="mw-redirect" title="Organization of Petroleum Exporting Countries">Organization of Petroleum Exporting Countries</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_the_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Transport in the Republic of the Congo">Transport in the Republic of the Congo</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Aeroport_Maya-Maya.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Aeroport_Maya-Maya.jpg/220px-Aeroport_Maya-Maya.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="110" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Aeroport_Maya-Maya.jpg/330px-Aeroport_Maya-Maya.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Aeroport_Maya-Maya.jpg/440px-Aeroport_Maya-Maya.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1194" data-file-height="596"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Aeroport_Maya-Maya.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Maya-Maya_Airport" title="Maya-Maya Airport">Maya-Maya Airport</a> in <a href="/wiki/Brazzaville" title="Brazzaville">Brazzaville</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Transport in the Republic of the Congo includes land, air and water transportation. The country's <a href="/wiki/Congo%E2%80%93Ocean_Railway" title="Congo–Ocean Railway">rail system</a> was <a href="/wiki/Congo%E2%80%93Ocean_Railway#History" title="Congo–Ocean Railway">built by forced laborers</a> during the 1930s and largely remains in operation. There are also over 1000&nbsp;km of paved roads and two major international airports (<a href="/wiki/Maya-Maya_Airport" title="Maya-Maya Airport">Maya-Maya Airport</a> and <a href="/wiki/Agostinho-Neto_International_Airport" title="Agostinho-Neto International Airport">Pointe-Noire Airport</a>) which have flights to destinations in Europe, Africa, and the Middle East. The country also has a large port on the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a> at <a href="/wiki/Pointe-Noire" title="Pointe-Noire">Pointe-Noire</a> and others along the <a href="/wiki/Congo_River" title="Congo River">Congo River</a> at <a href="/wiki/Brazzaville" title="Brazzaville">Brazzaville</a> and <a href="/wiki/Impfondo" title="Impfondo">Impfondo</a>. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_the_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Demographics of the Republic of the Congo">Demographics of the Republic of the Congo</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="PieChartTemplate thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px"> 
        <div style="background-color:white;margin:auto;position:relative;width:200px;height:200px;overflow:hidden;border-radius:100px;border:1px solid black"> 
         <div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:100px; top:100px; border-width:100px 0 0 15915.284869129px; border-left-color:black"></div>

      <p>The Republic of the Congo's sparse population is concentrated in the southwestern portion of the country, leaving the vast areas of tropical <a href="/wiki/Jungle" title="Jungle">jungle</a> in the north virtually uninhabited. Thus, Congo is one of the most urbanized countries in Africa, with 70% of its total population living in a few urban areas, namely in <a href="/wiki/Brazzaville" title="Brazzaville">Brazzaville</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pointe-Noire" title="Pointe-Noire">Pointe-Noire</a> or one of the small cities or villages lining the 534-kilometre (332&nbsp;mi) railway which connects the two cities. In rural areas, industrial and commercial activity has declined rapidly in recent years, leaving rural economies dependent on the government for support and subsistence.<sup id="cite_ref-StateDept_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-StateDept-67">[67]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Ethnically and linguistically the population of the Republic of the Congo is diverse—<a href="/wiki/Ethnologue" title="Ethnologue">Ethnologue</a> recognises 62 spoken languages in the country<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup>—but can be grouped into three categories. The <a href="/wiki/Kongo_people" title="Kongo people">Kongo</a> are the largest ethnic group and form roughly half of the population. The most significant subgroups of the Kongo are <a href="/wiki/Lari_(ethnic_group)" class="mw-redirect" title="Lari (ethnic group)">Laari</a>, in Brazzaville and Pool regions, and the <a href="/wiki/Vili_people" title="Vili people">Vili</a>, around Pointe-Noire and along the Atlantic coast. The second largest group are the <a href="/wiki/Bateke" class="mw-redirect" title="Bateke">Teke</a>, who live to the north of Brazzaville, with 17% of the population. <a href="/wiki/Mbochi" class="mw-redirect" title="Mbochi">Boulangui</a> (M’Boshi) live in the northwest and in Brazzaville and form 12% of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Pygmies" class="mw-redirect" title="Pygmies">Pygmies</a> make up 2% of Congo's population.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Before the 1997 war, about 9,000 <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europeans</a> and other non-Africans lived in Congo, most of whom were <a href="/wiki/French_people" title="French people">French</a>; only a fraction of this number remains.<sup id="cite_ref-StateDept_67-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-StateDept-67">[67]</a></sup> Around 300 <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">American</a> expatriates reside in the Congo.<sup id="cite_ref-StateDept_67-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-StateDept-67">[67]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>According to CIA World Factbook, the people of the Republic of the Congo are largely a mix of <a href="/wiki/Catholics" class="mw-redirect" title="Catholics">Catholics</a> (33.1%), <a href="/wiki/Awakening_(religious_movement)" class="mw-redirect" title="Awakening (religious movement)">Awakening Lutherans</a> (22.3%) and other <a href="/wiki/Protestants" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestants">Protestants</a> (19.9%). Followers of <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> make up 1.6%; this is primarily due to an influx of foreign workers into the urban centers.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-10">[10]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>According to a 2011–12 survey, total fertility rate was 5.1 children born per woman, with 4.5 in urban areas and 6.5 in rural areas.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> </p>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Health_in_the_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Health in the Republic of the Congo">Health in the Republic of the Congo</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Public expenditure health was at 8.9% of the GDP in 2004, whereas private expenditure was at 1.3%.<sup id="cite_ref-hdrstats.undp.org_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hdrstats.undp.org-73">[73]</a></sup> As of 2012<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the <a href="/wiki/HIV/AIDS" title="HIV/AIDS">HIV/AIDS</a> prevalence was at 2.8% among 15- to 49-year-olds.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_10-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-10">[10]</a></sup> Health expenditure was at US$30 per capita in 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-hdrstats.undp.org_73-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hdrstats.undp.org-73">[73]</a></sup> A large proportion of the population is undernourished,<sup id="cite_ref-hdrstats.undp.org_73-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hdrstats.undp.org-73">[73]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Malnutrition" title="Malnutrition">malnutrition</a> a problem in Congo-Brazzaville.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> There were 20 physicians per 100,000 persons in the early 2000s (decade).<sup id="cite_ref-hdrstats.undp.org_73-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hdrstats.undp.org-73">[73]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>As of 2010<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the <a href="/wiki/Maternal_mortality" class="mw-redirect" title="Maternal mortality">maternal mortality</a> rate was 560 deaths/100,000 live births, and the <a href="/wiki/Infant_mortality" title="Infant mortality">infant mortality</a> rate was 59.34 deaths/1,000 live births.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_10-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-10">[10]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Female_genital_mutilation" title="Female genital mutilation">Female genital mutilation</a> (FGM) is rare in the country, being confined to limited geographic areas of the country.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cultural_heritage">Cultural heritage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Cultural heritage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.<br><small><span class="plainlinks"><i>Find sources:</i>&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?as_eq=wikipedia&amp;q=%22Republic+of+the+Congo%22">"Republic of the Congo"</a>&nbsp;–&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbm=nws&amp;q=%22Republic+of+the+Congo%22+-wikipedia">news</a>&nbsp;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?&amp;q=%22Republic+of+the+Congo%22+site:news.google.com/newspapers&amp;source=newspapers">newspapers</a>&nbsp;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbs=bks:1&amp;q=%22Republic+of+the+Congo%22+-wikipedia">books</a>&nbsp;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//scholar.google.com/scholar?q=%22Republic+of+the+Congo%22">scholar</a>&nbsp;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.jstor.org/action/doBasicSearch?Query=%22Republic+of+the+Congo%22&amp;acc=on&amp;wc=on">JSTOR</a></span></small></span> <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">August 2017</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small>

        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_the_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Culture of the Republic of the Congo">Culture of the Republic of the Congo</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The Republic of the Congo has a wide variety of natural landscapes, ranging from the <a href="/wiki/Savanna" title="Savanna">savanna</a> plains in the North Niari flooded forests, to the vast Congo River, to rugged mountains and forest of <a href="/wiki/Mayombe" title="Mayombe">Mayombe</a>, and including 170&nbsp;km of beaches along the Atlantic coast.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> The numerous ethnic groups, forms of art, and political structures express a rich cultural diversity and </p>
      <p>Among the best known are <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Loango#Name" title="Kingdom of Loango">Vili</a> nail fetishes, <a href="/wiki/Bembe_people" title="Bembe people">Beembe</a> statuettes that are full of expression; the masks of the <a href="/wiki/Punu_people" title="Punu people">Punu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kwele_people" title="Kwele people">Kwele</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kota_people_(Gabon)" title="Kota people (Gabon)">Kota</a> reliquaries, <a href="/wiki/Teke_people" title="Teke people">Teke</a> fetishes, and cemeteries with monumental tombs are examples of this variety. The <a href="/wiki/Lari_people_(Congo)" title="Lari people (Congo)">Lari</a> people also have unique artifacts. </p>
      <p>The Republic of the Congo also has considerable colonial architectural heritage, which it is preserving. Restoration of architectural works is underway in Brazzaville, for example at the Basilica of Sainte-Anne du Congo, which was completed in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Because of problems with the communications network, the country is not ready to build on <a href="/wiki/Heritage_tourism" title="Heritage tourism">heritage tourism</a>. It is working to improve the network that supports its hotels and related tourism facilities in <a href="/wiki/Pointe_Noire" class="mw-redirect" title="Pointe Noire">Pointe Noire</a> and Brazzaville. Many sites are difficult to reach in overland visits. Some of the South's most populous and developed locations are often the least accessible. For example, the massive <a href="/wiki/Chaillu_Mountains" title="Chaillu Mountains">Chaillu Mountains</a> are almost impossible to visit. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Arts">Arts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Arts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="boilerplate metadata plainlinks tfd" id="tfd" style="background-color: transparent; padding: 0; font-size:xx-small; color:#000000; text-align: center; border-bottom:1px solid #AAAAAA; overflow:hidden;">
       ‹&nbsp;The <a href="/wiki/Help:Template" title="Help:Template">template</a> below (<i><a href="/wiki/Template:Rewrite_section" title="Template:Rewrite section">Rewrite section</a></i>) is being considered for merging. See <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Templates_for_discussion/Log/2021_February_1#Template:Rewrite_section" title="Wikipedia:Templates for discussion/Log/2021 February 1">templates for discussion</a> to help reach a consensus.&nbsp;›
      </div> 
      <div class="boilerplate metadata plainlinks tfd" id="tfd" style="background-color: transparent; padding: 0; font-size:xx-small; color:#000000; text-align: center; border-bottom:1px solid #AAAAAA; overflow:hidden;">
       ‹&nbsp;The <a href="/wiki/Help:Template" title="Help:Template">template</a> below (<i><a href="/wiki/Template:Cleanup_rewrite" title="Template:Cleanup rewrite">Cleanup rewrite</a></i>) is being considered for merging.
